[6/18/25, 9:55:11 PM] ཉི་འོད་🌅: Tashi Delek, Venerable Geshe La. 
We hope this message finds you well.

The current topic for the NIC1 Program is NIC104: Managing Life Challenges and Challenging Emotions - Buddhist Psychology and Rational Understanding of Operation of Law of Karma.

Venerable Geshe La began the session by revising what we had learned last time (Friday, 13th June 2025) and started with the question: "What is Mind?"— which Venerable Geshe La defined as a **clear and knowing agent**. Venerable Geshe La explained that the mind can be classified in various ways. One such classification is into **valid cognition** and **non-valid cognition**. Venerable Geshe La emphasized that we use the term *non-valid cognition* instead of *invalid cognition*, and there is a reason behind this specific usage.

Venerable Geshe La explained the Valid cognition in a general or loose sense, with a more detailed explanation to be covered under Buddhist Psychology, which will eventually be taught in the NCC eventually NDC. For those who are further interested, they can continue with the NMC which is a five-year program. However, Venerable Geshe La advised participants not to rush into the NMC. Instead, recommended beginning with the NCC, followed by the NDC, which spans a little over a year and explores Buddhist Psychology in more detail — including its various divisions and functions.

Venerable Geshe La said for the purpose of this current class — the **Nalanda Introductory Course (NIC)** — the focus is primarily on the **application** side of the teachings.

Venerable Geshe La then explained the **two types of mind**: valid and non-valid, using examples to illustrate each. Venerable Geshe La went on to describe the **Sevenfold Division of Mind**:

1. Direct Valid Perceiver
2. Inferential Cognizer
3. Subsequent Cognizer
4. Correctly Assuming Consciousness
5. Non-Discerning Direct Perceiver
6. Doubting Consciousness
7. Deceptive (Wrong) Consciousness

Venerable Geshe La noted that as the mind progresses **from number 7 up to number 1**, it becomes increasingly **finer and more refined**, moving away from suffering. Conversely, going **from 1 down to 7** increases suffering. Once the mind transforms into a **Direct Valid Perceiver**, mental defilements are gradually removed, leading one to the **PARAGATE** stage, followed by **PARASAMGATE BODHI SVAHA** — a state in which all miseries crumble away, and one attains **fearlessness and infinite happiness**.

Venerable Geshe La also spoke about the various types of Nalanda Courses offered by **Tibet House, New Delhi**.

Venerable Geshe La informed us that today’s session (Sunday, 15th June 2025) and the next one would focus on:
**“How Mental Emotions like Loneliness, Stress, Anxiety, and so forth Arise — and How to Tackle Them.”**
Venerable Geshe La advised that those who joined directly in the NIC1 program should pay special attention.

Venerable Geshe La then introduced the concept of the **"Fifty-One Mental Factors"**, which are divided into six categories:

1. Five Omnipresent Mental Factors
2. Five Object-Ascertaining (Determinative) Mental Factors
3. Eleven Virtuous Mental Factors
4. Six Root Afflictions
5. Twenty Secondary Afflictions
6. Four Variable Mental Factors

Venerable Geshe La said that we need to know why are there 51 mental factors and how are they divided into these categories?

Venerable Geshe La briefly explained each of the six divisions, but focused in detail on the **Five Omnipresent (Ever-Present) Mental Factors**, which are essential to understanding how emotions such as loneliness, anxiety, stress, and depression arise. These five factors are:

1. **Feeling**
2. **Discrimination**
3. **Intention**
4. **Contact**
5. **Attention**

However, Geshe La reorganized them in a different order to help better understand the mechanism of how disturbing emotions arise and how they can be reversed. The new order is:

1. **Contact**
2. **Attention**
3. **Discrimination**
4. **Feeling**
5. **Intention**

Venerable Geshe La explained why these are called **Omnipresent** and used an example to show how they operate in our minds. As part of the example, Venerable Geshe La also posed a question to the participants.

Venerable Geshe La concluded the session by stating that in the next class, we will do each of situations one by one including how to tackle loneliness, depression, anxiety, insecurity, laziness, and other related emotional challenges.

Thank you.

[7/24/25, 12:16:57 PM] ཉི་འོད་🌅: Launch of a NCC3 

Tibet House, Delhi is very happy to announce the launch of the third batch of Nalanda Certificate Course, NCC3 (22-week duration) on this joyous occasion of the 90th birthday of HH the 14th Dalai Lama. 

Teachings will be in English by Venerable Geshe Dorji Damdul La with simultaneous translation in Russian and Ladakhi.

Registration opens on 6th July 25 and teachings begin on 11th Aug 25.
 
For more details about this course, please visit Tibet House website - https://tibethouse.in/ncc

For any queries, please write to nalandacourses@tibethouse.in
